<p><b>Borneo</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>: <span lang="ms" xml:lang="ms"><i><b>Pulau Borneo</b></i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id" xml:lang="id"><i><b>Kalimantan</b></i></span>) is the third-<a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">largest island in the world</a> and the largest in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[note 1]</a></sup> At the geographic centre of <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">Maritime Southeast Asia</a>, in relation to major Indonesian islands, it is located north of <a href="/wiki/Java_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Java Island">Java</a>, west of <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>, and east of <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_divided_islands" title="List of divided islands">island is politically divided</a> among three countries: <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[1]</a></sup> Approximately 73% of the island is Indonesian territory. In the north, the <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">East Malaysian</a> states of <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> make up about 26% of the island. Additionally, the Malaysian federal territory of <a href="/wiki/Labuan" title="Labuan">Labuan</a> is situated on a small island just off the coast of Borneo. The sovereign state of <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, located on the north coast, comprises about 1% of Borneo's land area.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Antipodes" title="Antipodes">Antipodal</a> to an area of <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, Borneo is itself home to one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">rainforests</a> in the world.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The island is known by many names. Internationally it is known as <i>Borneo</i>, after <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire of Brunei">Brunei</a>, derived from European contact with the kingdom in the 16th century during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a>. The name <i>Brunei</i> possibly derives from the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> word "<i><span title="Sanskrit transliteration" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">váruṇa</span></i>" (<span lang="sa" xml:lang="sa">वरुण</span>), meaning either "water" or the mythological <a href="/wiki/Varuna" title="Varuna">Varuna</a>, the Hindu god of rain. <a href="/wiki/Native_Indonesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Indonesian">Indonesian natives</a> called it <i><a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>,</i> which was derived from the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> word <i>Kalamanthana,</i> meaning "burning weather island" (to describe its hot and humid <a href="/wiki/Tropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical">tropical</a> weather).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>In earlier times, the island was known by other names. In 977, <a href="/wiki/History_of_China" title="History of China">Chinese records</a> began to use the term <i>Po-ni</i> to refer to Borneo or Brunei. In 1225, it was also mentioned by the Chinese official <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Rugua" title="Zhao Rugua">Chau Ju-Kua</a> (趙汝适).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> The Javanese manuscript <a href="/wiki/Nagarakretagama" title="Nagarakretagama">Nagarakretagama</a>, written by <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> court poet <a href="/wiki/Mpu_Prapanca" title="Mpu Prapanca">Mpu Prapanca</a> in 1365, mentioned the island as <i>Nusa Tanjungnagara</i>, which means the island of the <a href="/wiki/Tanjungpura_Kingdom" title="Tanjungpura Kingdom">Tanjungpura Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geological_history_of_Borneo" title="Geological history of Borneo">Geological history of Borneo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg/220px-MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg/330px-MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg/440px-MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MountKinabalu_from_CheSuiKhorPagodaKK-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mount_Kinabalu" title="Mount Kinabalu">Mount Kinabalu</a> in Malaysia, the highest summit of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-highest_summit_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highest_summit-7">[6]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><span class="nowrap">Borneo is surrounded</span> by the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> to the north and northwest, the <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Sea" title="Sulu Sea">Sulu Sea</a> to the northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Celebes_Sea" title="Celebes Sea">Celebes Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Makassar_Strait" title="Makassar Strait">Makassar Strait</a> to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Java_Sea" title="Java Sea">Java Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karimata_Strait" title="Karimata Strait">Karimata Strait</a> to the south. To the west of Borneo are the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>. To the south and east are islands of Indonesia: <a href="/wiki/Java_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Java (island)">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>, respectively. To the northeast are the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippine Islands</a>. With an area of 743,330 square kilometres (287,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), it is the third-largest island in the world, and is the largest island of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> (the largest continent). Its highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kinabalu" title="Mount Kinabalu">Mount Kinabalu</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>, Malaysia, with an elevation of 4,095&#160;m (13,435&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-highest_summit_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highest_summit-7">[6]</a></sup> Before sea levels rose at the end of the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a>, Borneo was part of the mainland of Asia, forming, with <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, the upland regions of a peninsula that extended east from present day <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>. The <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a> now submerge the former low-lying areas of the peninsula. Deeper waters separating Borneo from neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a> prevented a land connection to that island, creating the divide known as <a href="/wiki/Wallace%27s_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Wallace's Line">Wallace's Line</a> between Asian and Australia-<a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> biological regions.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg/220px-Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg/330px-Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg/440px-Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scenery_around_Kapuas_River.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kapuas_River" title="Kapuas River">Kapuas River</a> in Indonesia, at 1,000&#160;km (620&#160;mi) in length, it is the longest river in Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-TanMerdikawati2015_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TanMerdikawati2015-10">[9]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest river system is the <a href="/wiki/Kapuas_River" title="Kapuas River">Kapuas</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a>, with a length of 1,000&#160;km (620&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-TanMerdikawati2015_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TanMerdikawati2015-10">[9]</a></sup> Other major rivers include the <a href="/wiki/Mahakam_River" title="Mahakam River">Mahakam</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East Kalimantan</a> (920&#160;km long (570&#160;mi)),<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Barito_River" title="Barito River">Barito</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Kalimantan" title="South Kalimantan">South Kalimantan</a> (900&#160;km long (560&#160;mi)),<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rajang_River" title="Rajang River">Rajang</a> in Sarawak (565&#160;km long (351&#160;mi))<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kinabatangan_River" title="Kinabatangan River">Kinabatangan</a> in Sabah (560&#160;km long (350&#160;mi)).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> Borneo has significant cave systems. In Sarawak, the Clearwater Cave has one of the world's longest underground rivers while <a href="/wiki/Deer_Cave" title="Deer Cave">Deer Cave</a> is home to over three million <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bats</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Guano" title="Guano">guano</a> accumulated to over 100 metres (330&#160;ft) deep.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gomantong_Caves" title="Gomantong Caves">Gomantong Caves</a> in Sabah has been dubbed as the "Cockroach Cave" due to the presence of million of cockroaches inside the cave.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gunung_Mulu_National_Park" title="Gunung Mulu National Park">Gunung Mulu National Park</a> in Sarawak and <a href="/wiki/Sangkulirang-Mangkalihat_Karst" title="Sangkulirang-Mangkalihat Karst">Sangkulirang-Mangkalihat Karst</a> in East Kalimantan which particularly a <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> areas contains thousands of smaller caves.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Borneo" title="Biodiversity of Borneo">Biodiversity of Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Borneo" title="Fauna of Borneo">Fauna of Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Borneo" title="Flora of Borneo">Flora of Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_endemic_birds_of_Borneo" title="List of endemic birds of Borneo">List of endemic birds of Borneo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mammals_of_Borneo" title="Mammals of Borneo">Mammals of Borneo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg/220px-Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg/330px-Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg/440px-Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4400" data-file-height="5800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Borneo_19_May_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> satellite image of Borneo on 19 May 2002.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Borneo <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> is estimated to be around 140 million years old, making it one of the oldest rainforests in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> It is the centre of the evolution and distribution of many <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species of plants and animals, and the rainforest is one of the few remaining <a href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitat (ecology)">natural habitats</a> for the endangered <a href="/wiki/Bornean_orangutan" title="Bornean orangutan">Bornean orangutan</a>. It is an important refuge for many endemic forest species, including the <a href="/wiki/Borneo_elephant" title="Borneo elephant">Borneo elephant</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Sumatran_rhinoceros" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Sumatran rhinoceros">eastern Sumatran rhinoceros</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bornean_clouded_leopard" class="mw-redirect" title="Bornean clouded leopard">Bornean clouded leopard</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hose%27s_palm_civet" title="Hose's palm civet">hose's palm civet</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dayak_fruit_bat" title="Dayak fruit bat">dayak fruit bat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Borneo_peat_swamp_forests" title="Borneo peat swamp forests">Peat swamp forests</a> occupy the entire coastline of Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The soil of the peat swamp are comparatively infertile, while it is known to be the home of various bird species such as the <a href="/wiki/Hook-billed_bulbul" title="Hook-billed bulbul">hook-billed bulbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmeted_hornbill" title="Helmeted hornbill">helmeted hornbill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros_hornbill" title="Rhinoceros hornbill">rhinoceros hornbill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> There are about 15,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> with 3,000 species of trees (267 species are <a href="/wiki/Dipterocarp" class="mw-redirect" title="Dipterocarp">dipterocarps</a>), 221 species of terrestrial mammals and 420 species of resident birds in Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> There are about 440 freshwater fish species in Borneo (about the same as Sumatra and Java combined).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a> (WWF) stated that 123 species have been discovered in Borneo since the "<a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Borneo" title="Heart of Borneo">Heart of Borneo</a>" agreement was signed in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg/220px-Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg/330px-Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg/440px-Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="945" data-file-height="627" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kepin_-_Kevin_taking_a_nap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Bornean_orangutan" title="Bornean orangutan">Bornean orangutan</a>, a great ape <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> to Borneo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The WWF has classified the island into seven distinct <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>. Most are lowland regions:<sup id="cite_ref-Borneo_forests_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borneo_forests-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Borneo_lowland_rain_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Borneo lowland rain forests">Borneo lowland rain forests</a> cover most of the island, with an area of 427,500 square kilometres (165,100&#160;sq&#160;mi);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Borneo_peat_swamp_forests" title="Borneo peat swamp forests">Borneo peat swamp forests</a>;</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Kerangas" class="mw-redirect" title="Kerangas">Kerangas</a></i> or Sundaland heath forests;</li>
<li>Southwest Borneo freshwater swamp forests; and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sunda_Shelf_mangroves" title="Sunda Shelf mangroves">Sunda Shelf mangroves</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Borneo_montane_rain_forests" title="Borneo montane rain forests">Borneo montane rain forests</a> lie in the central highlands of the island, above the 1,000 metres (3,300&#160;ft) elevation.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands</a> on South Kalimantan.</li>
</ul>
<p>The highest elevations of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kinabalu" title="Mount Kinabalu">Mount Kinabalu</a> are home to the Kinabalu mountain <a href="/wiki/Alpine_meadow" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine meadow">alpine meadow</a>, an alpine shrubland notable for its numerous endemic species, including many orchids.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_issues">Conservation issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Conservation issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Borneo" title="Deforestation in Borneo">Deforestation in Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_Indonesian_forest_fires" title="1997 Indonesian forest fires">1997 Indonesian forest fires</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="1997 Southeast Asian haze">1997 Southeast Asian haze</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2006 Southeast Asian haze">2006 Southeast Asian haze</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2013 Southeast Asian haze">2013 Southeast Asian haze</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2015 Southeast Asian haze">2015 Southeast Asian haze</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2016 Southeast Asian haze">2016 Southeast Asian haze</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg/220px-Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg/330px-Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg/440px-Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Logging_road_East_Kalimantan_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logging road in <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East Kalimantan</a>, Indonesia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The island historically had extensive rainforest cover, but the area was reduced due to heavy <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a> by the Indonesian and Malaysian wood industry, especially with the large demands of raw materials from <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">industrial countries</a> along with the conversion of forest lands for large-scale agricultural purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-Borneo_forests_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borneo_forests-27">[26]</a></sup> Half of the annual global <a href="/wiki/Tropical_timber" title="Tropical timber">tropical timber</a> acquisition comes from Borneo. <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">Palm oil</a> plantations have been widely developed and are rapidly encroaching on the last remnants of primary rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">Forest fires</a> since 1997, started by the locals to clear the forests for plantations were exacerbated by an exceptionally dry <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a> season, worsening the annual shrinkage of the rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> During these fires, hotspots were visible on <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">satellite images</a> and resulting <a href="/wiki/Haze" title="Haze">haze</a> that frequently affecting Brunei, Indonesia, Malaysia, Singapore and if turns much worse the haze will also reaching to southern <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> as evidenced on the <a href="/wiki/2015_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2015 Southeast Asian haze">2015 Southeast Asian haze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg/220px-Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg/330px-Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg/440px-Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3930" data-file-height="2544" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dayaks_in_their_war_dress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a>, the main <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous people">indigenous people</a> in the island.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_territorial_lose_(1400%E2%80%931890).gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif/220px-Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif/330px-Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif/440px-Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="225" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_territorial_lose_(1400%E2%80%931890).gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Territorial loss of the <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">thalassocracy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Sultanate of Brunei</a> from 1400 to 1890 due to the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Western_imperialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Western imperialism">Western imperialism</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to ancient Chinese (977),<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:129</sup> Indian and Japanese manuscripts, western coastal cities of Borneo had become trading ports by the first millennium AD.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> In Chinese manuscripts, gold, <a href="/wiki/Camphor" title="Camphor">camphor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortoise" title="Tortoise">tortoise</a> shells, <a href="/wiki/Hornbill_ivory" title="Hornbill ivory">hornbill ivory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a> horn, <a href="/wiki/Crane_(bird)" title="Crane (bird)">crane crest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beeswax" title="Beeswax">beeswax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakawood" title="Lakawood">lakawood</a> (a scented heartwood and root wood of a thick <a href="/wiki/Liana" title="Liana">liana</a>, <i>Dalbergia parviflora</i>), <a href="/wiki/Dragon%27s_blood" title="Dragon's blood">dragon's blood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rattan" title="Rattan">rattan</a>, edible <a href="/wiki/Bird%27s_nest_soup" class="mw-redirect" title="Bird's nest soup">bird's nests</a> and various spices were described as among the most valuable items from Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-Broek1962_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broek1962-35">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_India" title="Demographics of India">Indians</a> named Borneo <i>Suvarnabhumi</i> (the land of gold) and also <i>Karpuradvipa</i> (Camphor Island). The <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> named Borneo <i>Puradvipa</i>, or Diamond Island. <a href="/wiki/Archaeological" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological">Archaeological</a> findings in the Sarawak river delta reveal that the area was a thriving centre of trade between India and China from the 6th century until about 1300.<sup id="cite_ref-Broek1962_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broek1962-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Stone pillars bearing inscriptions in the <a href="/wiki/Pallava_script" title="Pallava script">Pallava script</a>, found in <a href="/wiki/Kutai" title="Kutai">Kutai</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Mahakam_River" title="Mahakam River">Mahakam River</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East Kalimantan</a> and dating to around the second half of the 4th century, constitute some of the oldest evidence of <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> influence in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> By the 14th century, Borneo became a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> (in present-day Indonesia),<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> later changing its allegiance to the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> of China.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> The religion of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> entered the island in the 10th century,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> following the arrival of Muslim traders who later converted many indigenous peoples in the coastal areas.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Sultanate of Brunei declared independence from Majapahit following the death of Majapahit Emperor in mid-14th century. During its golden age under <a href="/wiki/Bolkiah" title="Bolkiah">Bolkiah</a> from the 15th century to the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Bruneian Empire</a> ruled almost entire coastal area of Borneo (lending its name to the island due to its influence in the region) and several islands in the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> During the 1450s, <a href="/wiki/Sharif_ul-H%C4%81shim_of_Sulu" title="Sharif ul-Hāshim of Sulu">Shari'ful Hashem Syed Abu Bakr</a>, an Arab born in <a href="/wiki/Johor" title="Johor">Johor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> arrived in Sulu from Malacca. In 1457, he founded the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Sulu" title="Sultanate of Sulu">Sultanate of Sulu</a>; he titled himself as "Paduka Maulana Mahasari Sharif Sultan Hashem Abu Bakr".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Following their independence in 1578 from Brunei's influence,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> the Sulu's began to expand their <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">thalassocracy</a> to parts of the northern Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hussainmiya2006_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hussainmiya2006-47">[46]</a></sup> Both the sultanates who ruled northern Borneo had traditionally engaged in trade with China by means of the frequently-arriving Chinese <a href="/wiki/Junk_(ship)" title="Junk (ship)">junks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Despite the thalassocracy of the sultanates, Borneo's interior region remained free from the rule of any kingdoms.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_and_Dutch_control">British and Dutch control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: British and Dutch control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_Borneo" title="British Borneo">British Borneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan,_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan%2C_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg/220px-Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan%2C_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan%2C_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg/330px-Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan%2C_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan%2C_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg/440px-Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan%2C_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="784" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceremony_of_Hoisting_the_British_Flag_on_the_island_of_Labuan,_N._W._Coast_of_Borneo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">British flag</a> hoisted for the first time on the island of <a href="/wiki/Labuan" title="Labuan">Labuan</a> on 24 December 1846.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Malacca_(1511)" title="Capture of Malacca (1511)">fall of Malacca</a> in 1511, Portuguese merchants traded regularly with Borneo, and especially with Brunei from 1530.<sup id="cite_ref-Lach1994_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lach1994-51">[50]</a></sup> Having visited Brunei's capital, the Portuguese described the place as surrounded by a <a href="/wiki/Stone_wall" title="Stone wall">stone wall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> While Borneo was seen as rich, the Portuguese did not make any attempts to conquer it.<sup id="cite_ref-Lach1994_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lach1994-51">[50]</a></sup> The Spanish visit to Brunei led to the <a href="/wiki/Castilian_War" title="Castilian War">Castilian War</a> in 1578. The English began to trade with <a href="/wiki/Sambas" class="mw-disambig" title="Sambas">Sambas</a> of southern Borneo in 1609, while the Dutch only began their trade in 1644: to Banjar and Martapura, also in the southern Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> The Dutch tried to settle the island of <a href="/wiki/Balambangan_Island" title="Balambangan Island">Balambangan</a>, north of Borneo, in the second half of the 18th century, but withdrew by 1797.<sup id="cite_ref-Dutch_Borneo_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dutch_Borneo-54">[53]</a></sup> In 1812, the sultan in southern Borneo ceded his forts to the <a href="/wiki/English_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="English East India Company">English East India Company</a>. The English, led by <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Raffles" title="Stamford Raffles">Stamford Raffles</a>, then tried to establish an intervention in Sambas but failed. Although they managed to defeat the Sultanate the next year and declared a blockade on all ports in Borneo except Brunei, <a href="/wiki/Banjarmasin" title="Banjarmasin">Banjarmasin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a>, the project was cancelled by the British Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Elliot-Murray-Kynynmound,_1st_Earl_of_Minto" title="Gilbert Elliot-Murray-Kynynmound, 1st Earl of Minto">Lord Minto</a> in India as it was too expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-Dutch_Borneo_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dutch_Borneo-54">[53]</a></sup> At the beginning of British and Dutch exploration on the island, they described the island of Borneo as full of <a href="/wiki/Headhunting" title="Headhunting">head hunters</a>, with the indigenous in the interior practising <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannibalism">cannibalism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Dutch_and_British_explorations_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dutch_and_British_explorations-55">[54]</a></sup> and the waters around the island infested with <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a>, especially between the north eastern Borneo and the southern Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malay_race" title="Malay race">Malay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iban_people" title="Iban people">Sea Dayak</a> pirates preyed on maritime shipping in the waters between Singapore and Hong Kong from their haven in Borneo,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> along with the attacks by <a href="/wiki/Illanun" class="mw-redirect" title="Illanun">Illanuns</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Moro_Pirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Moro Pirates">Moro Pirates</a> from the southern Philippines, such as in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_off_Mukah" title="Battle off Mukah">Battle off Mukah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_and_Dutch_Borneo,_1898.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/British_and_Dutch_Borneo%2C_1898.png/220px-British_and_Dutch_Borneo%2C_1898.png" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/British_and_Dutch_Borneo%2C_1898.png/330px-British_and_Dutch_Borneo%2C_1898.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/British_and_Dutch_Borneo%2C_1898.png/440px-British_and_Dutch_Borneo%2C_1898.png 2x" data-file-width="580" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_and_Dutch_Borneo,_1898.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the island divided between the British and the Dutch, 1898. The present boundaries of Malaysia, Indonesia and Brunei are largely inherited from the British and Dutch colonial rules.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Dutch began to intervene in the southern part of the island upon resuming contact in 1815, posting <a href="/wiki/Resident_(title)" title="Resident (title)">Residents</a> to Banjarmasin, Pontianak and Sambas and Assistant-Residents to Landak and Mampawa.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> The Sultanate of Brunei in 1842 granted large parts of land in Sarawak to the English adventurer <a href="/wiki/James_Brooke" title="James Brooke">James Brooke</a>, as a reward for his help in quelling a local rebellion. Brooke established the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sarawak" title="Kingdom of Sarawak">Kingdom of Sarawak</a> and was recognised as its rajah after paying a fee to the Sultanate. He established a monarchy, and the Brooke dynasty (through his nephew and great-nephew) ruled Sarawak for 100 years; the leaders were known as the <a href="/wiki/White_Rajahs" title="White Rajahs">White Rajahs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> Brooke also acquired the island of <a href="/wiki/Labuan" title="Labuan">Labuan</a> for <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Britain</a> in 1846 through the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Labuan" title="Treaty of Labuan">Treaty of Labuan</a> with the Sultan of Brunei, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_II" title="Omar Ali Saifuddin II">Omar Ali Saifuddin II</a> on 18 December 1846.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The region of northern Borneo came under the administration of <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo_Chartered_Company" title="North Borneo Chartered Company">North Borneo Chartered Company</a> following the acquisition of territory from the Sultanates of Brunei and Sulu by a German businessman and adventurer named <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Overbeck" title="Gustav Overbeck">Baron von Overbeck</a>, before it was passed to British Dent brothers (comprising <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Dent" title="Alfred Dent">Alfred Dent</a> and Edward Dent).<sup id="cite_ref-Hussainmiya2006_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hussainmiya2006-47">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Further enroachment by the British reduced the territory of Brunei.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> This led the 26th Sultan of Brunei, <a href="/wiki/Hashim_Jalilul_Alam_Aqamaddin" title="Hashim Jalilul Alam Aqamaddin">Hashim Jalilul Alam Aqamaddin</a> to appeal the British to stop, and as a result a Treaty of Protection was signed in 1888, rendering Brunei a British protectorate.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg/220px-1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg" width="220" height="378" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg/330px-1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg/440px-1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1720" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1916_Dutch_East_Indies_-_Art.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dutch imperial imagery representing the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (1916). The text reads "Our most precious jewel" which includes the whole island of Borneo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before the acquisition by the British, the Americans also managed to establish their temporary presence in northwestern Borneo after acquiring a parcel of land from the Sultanate of Brunei. A company known as <a href="/wiki/American_Trading_Company_of_Borneo" title="American Trading Company of Borneo">American Trading Company of Borneo</a> was formed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_William_Torrey" title="Joseph William Torrey">Joseph William Torrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bradley_Harris" title="Thomas Bradley Harris">Thomas Bradley Harris</a> and several Chinese investors, establishing a colony named "Ellena" in the <a href="/wiki/Kimanis" title="Kimanis">Kimanis</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> The colony failed and was abandoned, due to denials of financial backing, especially by the US government, and to diseases and riots among the workers.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Before Torrey left, he managed to sell the land to the German businessman, Overbeck.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Germans under William Frederick Schuck was awarded a parcel of land in northeastern Borneo of the Sandakan Bay from the Sultanate of Sulu where he operate business and export large quantities of arms, <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a>, textiles and tobacco to Sulu before the land were also passed to Overbeck by the Sultanate.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the recognition of Spanish presence in the Philippine archipelago, a protocol known as the <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Protocol_of_1885" title="Madrid Protocol of 1885">Madrid Protocol of 1885</a> was signed between the governments of the United Kingdom, Germany and Spain in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> to cement Spanish influence and recognise their sovereignty over the Sultanate of Sulu—in return for Spain's relinquishing its claim to the former possessions of the Sultanate in northern Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> The British administration then established the first railway network in northern Borneo, known as the <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="North Borneo Railway">North Borneo Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> During this time, the British sponsored a large number of Chinese workers to migrate to northern Borneo to work in European plantation and mines,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> and the Dutch followed suit to increase their economic production.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> By 1888, North Borneo, Sarawak and Brunei in northern Borneo had become British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PrescottTriggs2008_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrescottTriggs2008-78">[77]</a></sup> The area in southern Borneo was made Dutch protectorate in 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-Dutch_and_British_explorations_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dutch_and_British_explorations-55">[54]</a></sup> The Dutch who already claimed the whole Borneo were asked by Britain to delimit their boundaries between the two colonial territories to avoid further conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-PrescottTriggs2008_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrescottTriggs2008-78">[77]</a></sup> The British and Dutch governments had signed the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Treaty_of_1824" title="Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1824">Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1824</a> to exchange trading ports in <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> that were under their controls and assert spheres of influence. This resulted in indirectly establishing British- and Dutch-controlled areas in the north (Malay Peninsula) and south (Sumatra and Riau Islands) respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_British_Borneo" title="Japanese occupation of British Borneo">Japanese occupation of British Borneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies">Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies</a></div>

Japanese troops march through the streets of <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Labuan" title="Crown Colony of Labuan">Labuan</a> on 14 January 1942.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Australian_Support_Craft_(AWM_108818).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Australian_Support_Craft_%28AWM_108818%29.JPG/220px-Australian_Support_Craft_%28AWM_108818%29.JPG" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Australian_Support_Craft_%28AWM_108818%29.JPG/330px-Australian_Support_Craft_%28AWM_108818%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Australian_Support_Craft_%28AWM_108818%29.JPG/440px-Australian_Support_Craft_%28AWM_108818%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="501" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Australian_Support_Craft_(AWM_108818).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Australian <a href="/wiki/Landing_craft" title="Landing craft">support craft</a> moving towards <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Labuan" title="Victoria, Labuan">Victoria</a> and Brown beach to assist the landing of the members of <a href="/wiki/24th_Brigade_(Australia)" title="24th Brigade (Australia)">24th Infantry Brigade</a> on the island during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Oboe_Six" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Oboe Six">Operation Oboe Six</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During World War II, Japanese forces gained control and occupied most areas of Borneo from 1941–45. In the first stage of the war, the British saw the Japanese advance to Borneo as motivated by political and territorial ambitions rather than economic factors.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> The occupation drove many people in the coastal towns to the interior, searching for food and escaping the Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-Lim2008_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lim2008-81">[80]</a></sup> The Chinese residents in Borneo, especially with the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Sino-Japanese War</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a> mostly resisted the Japanese occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> Following the formation of resistance movements in northern Borneo such as the <a href="/wiki/Jesselton_Revolt" title="Jesselton Revolt">Jesselton Revolt</a>, many innocent indigenous and Chinese people were executed by the Japanese for their alleged involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Kalimantan, the Japanese also killed many Malay intellectuals, executing all the Malay Sultans of West Kalimantan in the <a href="/wiki/Pontianak_incidents" title="Pontianak incidents">Pontianak incidents</a>, together with Chinese people who were already against the Japanese for suspecting them to be threats.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> Sultan <a href="/w/index.php?title=Muhammad_Ibrahim_Shafi_ud-din_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Muhammad Ibrahim Shafi ud-din II (page does not exist)">Muhammad Ibrahim Shafi ud-din II</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Sambas" title="Sultanate of Sambas">Sambas</a> was executed in 1944. The Sultanate was thereafter suspended and replaced by a Japanese council.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> The Japanese also set-up <i>Pusat Tenaga Rakjat</i> (PUTERA)<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> in the Indonesian archipelago in 1943, although it was abolished the following year when it become too nationalistic.<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer2000_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer2000-87">[86]</a></sup> Some of the Indonesian nationalist like <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Hatta" title="Mohammad Hatta">Hatta</a> who had returned from Dutch exile began to co-operate with the Japanese. Shortly after his release, Sukarno became President of the Central Advisory Council, an advisory council for south Borneo, <a href="/wiki/Celebes_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Celebes Islands">Celebes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Sunda_Islands" title="Lesser Sunda Islands">Lesser Sunda</a>, set up in February 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer2000_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer2000-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Singapore" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of Singapore">fall of Singapore</a>, the Japanese sent several thousand of British and Australian <a href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Prisoners of war">prisoners of war</a> to camps in Borneo such as <a href="/wiki/Batu_Lintang_camp" title="Batu Lintang camp">Batu Lintang camp</a>. From the <a href="/wiki/Sandakan_camp" title="Sandakan camp">Sandakan camp</a> site, only six of some 2,500 prisoners survived after they were forced to march in an event known as the <a href="/wiki/Sandakan_Death_March" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandakan Death March">Sandakan Death March</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> In addition, of the total of 17,488 <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> labourers brought in by the Japanese during the occupation, only 1,500 survived mainly due to starvation, harsh working conditions and maltreatment.<sup id="cite_ref-Lim2008_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lim2008-81">[80]</a></sup> The Dayak and other indigenous people played a role in <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> against the occupying forces, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Kapit_Division" title="Kapit Division">Kapit Division</a>. They temporarily revived headhunting of Japanese toward the end of the war,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> with Allied <a href="/wiki/Z_Special_Unit" title="Z Special Unit">Z Special Unit</a> provided assistance to them.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> Australia contributed significantly to the liberation of Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_Australian_Imperial_Force" title="Second Australian Imperial Force">Australian Imperial Force</a> was sent to Borneo to fight off the Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Together with other Allies, the island <a href="/wiki/Borneo_campaign_(1945)" title="Borneo campaign (1945)">was completely liberated</a> in 1945.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan,_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan%2C_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg/220px-Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan%2C_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan%2C_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg/330px-Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan%2C_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan%2C_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg/440px-Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan%2C_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2561" data-file-height="1679" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sukarno_with_adat_people_in_West_Kalimantan,_Bung_Karno_Penjambung_Lidah_Rakjat_252.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> visiting <a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a> in 1963.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Towards the end of the war, Japan decided to give an early independence to a new proposed country of Indonesia on 17 July 1945, with an Independence Committee meeting scheduled for 19 August 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer2000_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer2000-87">[86]</a></sup> However, following the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrender of Japan</a> to the Allied forces, the meeting was shelved. Sukarno and Hatta continued the plan by unilaterally declaring independence, although the Dutch tried to retake their colonial possession in Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer2000_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer2000-87">[86]</a></sup> The southern part of the island achieved its independence through the <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_Indonesian_Independence" title="Proclamation of Indonesian Independence">Proclamation of Indonesian Independence</a> on 17 August 1945. The reaction was relatively muted with little open fighting in Pontianak or in the Chinese majority areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Heidhues2003_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heidhues2003-93">[92]</a></sup> While nationalist guerrillas supporting the inclusion of southern Borneo in the new Indonesian republic were active in Ketapang, and to lesser extent in Sambas where they rallied with the red-white flag which became the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Indonesia" title="Flag of Indonesia">flag of Indonesia</a>, most of the Chinese residents in southern Borneo expected to be liberate by <a href="/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army" title="National Revolutionary Army">Chinese Nationalist troops</a> from Mainland China and to integrate their districts as an overseas province of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912–49)">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Heidhues2003_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heidhues2003-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1945, officials in Tokyo suggested that whether northern Borneo should be included in the proposed new country of Indonesia should be separately determined based on the desires of its indigenous people and following the disposition of <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">Malaya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> Sukarno and <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Yamin" title="Mohammad Yamin">Mohammad Yamin</a> meanwhile continuously advocated for a <a href="/wiki/Greater_Indonesia" title="Greater Indonesia">Greater Indonesian</a> republic.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> As the President of the new republic, perceiving the British trying to maintain their presence in northern Borneo and Malay Peninsula, he decided to launch a military infiltration later known as the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation">confrontation</a> between 1962 until 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> In 1961, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tunku_Abdul_Rahman" title="Tunku Abdul Rahman">Tunku Abdul Rahman</a> of the independent <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Federation of Malaya</a> desired to unite Malaya, the British colonies of <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Sarawak" title="Crown Colony of Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Singapore" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Colony of Singapore">Singapore</a> and the Protectorate of <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a> under the proposed <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation of Malaysia">Federation of Malaysia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> The idea was heavily opposed by the governments in both Indonesia and the Philippines as well from Communist sympathisers and nationalist in Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> As a response to the growing opposition, the British deployed their armed forces to guard their colonies against Indonesian and communist revolts,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> which was also participated by Australia and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg/220px-Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg/330px-Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg/440px-Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="725" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_searching_for_enemies_during_a_patrol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Own_Highlanders_(Seaforth_and_Camerons)" title="Queen's Own Highlanders (Seaforth and Camerons)">Queen's Own Highlanders</a> 1st Battalion conduct a patrol to search for enemy positions in the jungle of Brunei.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Philippines opposed the newly proposed federation, claiming the eastern part of North Borneo (today the Malaysian state of Sabah) as part of its territory as a former possession of the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Sulu" title="Sultanate of Sulu">Sultanate of Sulu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> The Philippine government mostly based their claim on the Sultanate of Sulu's <a href="/wiki/Cession" title="Cession">cession</a> agreement with the British North Borneo Company, as by now the Sultanate had come under the jurisdiction of the Philippine republican administration, which therefore should inherit the Sulu former territories. The Philippine government also claimed that the heirs of the Sultanate had ceded all their territorial rights to the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Sultanate of Brunei at the first welcomed the proposal of a new larger federation.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_People%27s_Party" title="Brunei People's Party">Brunei People's Party</a> led by <a href="/wiki/A.M._Azahari" class="mw-redirect" title="A.M. Azahari">A.M. Azahari</a> desired to reunify Brunei, Sarawak and North Borneo into one federation known as the <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo_Federation" title="North Borneo Federation">North Borneo Federation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>: <span lang="ms" xml:lang="ms"><i>Kesatuan Negara Kalimantan Utara</i></span>), where the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sultans_of_Brunei" title="List of Sultans of Brunei">Sultan of Brunei</a> would be the head of state for the federation—though Azahari had his own intention to abolish the Brunei Monarchy, to make Brunei more democratic, and to integrate the territory and other former British colonies in Borneo into Indonesia, with the support from the latter government.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> This directly led to the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei Revolt">Brunei Revolt</a>, which thwarted Azahari's attempt and forced him to escape to Indonesia. Brunei withdrew from being part of the new Federation of Malaysia due to some disagreements on other issues while political leaders in Sarawak and North Borneo continued to favour inclusion in a larger federation.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the continuous opposition from Indonesia and the Philippines, the <a href="/wiki/Cobbold_Commission" title="Cobbold Commission">Cobbold Commission</a> was established to discover the feeling of the native populations in northern Borneo; it found the people greatly in favour of federation, with various stipulations.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The federation was successfully achieved with the inclusion of northern Borneo through the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Agreement" title="Malaysia Agreement">Malaysia Agreement</a> on 16 September 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Until present, the area in northern Borneo still subjected to attacks by Moro Pirates since the 18th century, and militants such as the <a href="/wiki/Abu_Sayyaf" title="Abu Sayyaf">Abu Sayyaf</a> since 2000 in the frequent <a href="/wiki/Cross_border_attacks_in_Sabah" title="Cross border attacks in Sabah">cross border attacks</a>. During the administration of Philippine President of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Marcos" title="Ferdinand Marcos">Ferdinand Marcos</a>, the President made some attempts to destabilise the state of Sabah,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> although his plan failed and resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Jabidah_massacre" title="Jabidah massacre">Jabidah massacre</a> and later in <a href="/wiki/Moro_conflict" title="Moro conflict">insurgency in the southern Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:138px;max-width:138px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:90px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:YanAriefSapeh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/YanAriefSapeh.jpg/136px-YanAriefSapeh.jpg" width="136" height="102" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/YanAriefSapeh.jpg/204px-YanAriefSapeh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/YanAriefSapeh.jpg/272px-YanAriefSapeh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:150px;max-width:150px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:90px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg/148px-KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg" width="148" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg/222px-KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg/296px-KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:290px;max-width:290px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:191px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg/288px-KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg" width="288" height="192" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg/432px-KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg/576px-KgKuaiKandazon_Sabah_Monsopiad-Cultural-Village-DansePerformance-16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Indigenous peoples with their <a href="/wiki/Folk_instrument" title="Folk instrument">music instrument</a>, dance and their respective <a href="/wiki/Folk_costume" title="Folk costume">traditional dress</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> for Borneo is <b>Bornean</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Borneo has 19.8 million inhabitants (in mid-2010), a population density of 26 inhabitants per square km. Most of the population lives in coastal cities, although the hinterland has small towns and villages along the rivers. The population consists mainly of <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a> ethnic groups, <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banjar_people" title="Banjar people">Banjar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orang_Ulu" title="Orang Ulu">Orang Ulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kadazan-Dusun" title="Kadazan-Dusun">Kadazan-Dusun</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a>, who make up 29% of the population of <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> and 17% of total population in <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a>, Indonesia<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> are descendants of immigrants primarily from southeastern China.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Sabah during the administration of <a href="/wiki/Mustapha_Harun" title="Mustapha Harun">Mustapha Harun</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Sabah_National_Organisation" title="United Sabah National Organisation">United Sabah National Organisation</a> (USNO) in the 1970s, thousands of Muslim immigrants and refugees from the southern Philippines of <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a> of Indonesia were given sanctuary and later <a href="/wiki/Identity_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Identity card">identity cards</a> in the bid to increase the Muslim population of the state: a policy later known as <a href="/wiki/Project_IC" title="Project IC">Project IC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> Due to the high number of crimes attributed to the new migrant populations, <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_tension" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic tension">ethnic tension</a> between the indigenous and migrant populations has risen up to the present.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Kalimantan since the 1990s, the Indonesian government has undertaken an intense <a href="/wiki/Transmigration_program" title="Transmigration program">transmigration program</a>; to that end it has financed the relocation of poor, landless families from Java, Madura, and Bali. By 2001, transmigrants made up 21% of the population in <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalimantan" title="Central Kalimantan">Central Kalimantan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Since the 1990s, the indigenous Dayak and Malays have resisted encroachment by these migrants, and violent conflict has occurred between some transmigrant and indigenous populations. In the 1999 <a href="/wiki/Sambas_riots" title="Sambas riots">Sambas riots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayaks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Malays" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Malays">Malays</a> joined together to massacre thousands of the <a href="/wiki/Madurese_people" title="Madurese people">Madurese</a> migrants. In Kalimantan, thousands were killed in 2001 fighting between <a href="/wiki/Madurese_transmigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Madurese transmigrant">Madurese transmigrants</a> and the Dayak people in the <a href="/wiki/Sampit_conflict" title="Sampit conflict">Sampit conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is a list of 20 largest <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a> in Borneo by population, based on 2010 census for Indonesia<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> and 2010 census for Malaysia.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> Population data signifies number within official districts and does not include adjoining or nearby <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> outside defined districts—such as Kota Kinabalu and Banjarbaru. In other instances, the district area is much larger than the actual city it represents thereby relatively inflating the population estimate by including the surrounding rural population—in cases such as Tawau and Palangkaraya.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto;" width="70%">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Borneo2_map_english_names.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Borneo2_map_english_names.svg/220px-Borneo2_map_english_names.svg.png" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Borneo2_map_english_names.svg/330px-Borneo2_map_english_names.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Borneo2_map_english_names.svg/440px-Borneo2_map_english_names.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1063" data-file-height="1183" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Borneo2_map_english_names.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Political divisions of Borneo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The island of Borneo is divided administratively by three countries.</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Kalimantan" title="South Kalimantan">South</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Kalimantan" title="North Kalimantan">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalimantan" title="Central Kalimantan">Central Kalimantan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/States_of_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="States of Malaysia">Malaysian states</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> (The Malaysian <a href="/wiki/Federal_Territory_(Malaysia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Territory (Malaysia)">Federal Territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Labuan_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Labuan Territory">Labuan</a> is located on nearshore islands of Borneo.)</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Borneo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Borneo's economy depends mainly on agriculture, logging and mining, <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">oil</a> and gas, and <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Borneo_economy_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borneo_economy-127">[126]</a></sup> Brunei's economy is highly dependent on the oil and gas production sector, and the country has become one of the largest oil producers in Southeast Asia. The Malaysian states of Sabah and Sarawak are both top exporters of <a href="/wiki/Timber" class="mw-redirect" title="Timber">timber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Borneo_economy_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borneo_economy-127">[126]</a></sup> Sabah is also known as the agricultural producer of <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">rubber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theobroma_cacao" title="Theobroma cacao">cacao</a>, and vegetables, and for its fisheries, while both Sabah and Sarawak export <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a> (LNG) and petroleum. The Indonesian provinces of Kalimantan are mostly dependent on <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a> sectors despite also being involved in logging and oil and gas explorations.<sup id="cite_ref-Borneo_economy_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borneo_economy-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
